  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_40a6b10d-9096-4ce0-8d4f-64930be9b30e'
      });

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1798321857" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11226148834945151260">1946 Newbery Medal winner.<br/><br/>These older Newbery Medal books, these children's classics, are struggling to stand the test of time. Why? Well, take this one for example. It's about a time gone by, very different from today, a much harder time. It's characters, it's language, it's life situations are so stark, they must seem almost foreign to today's young readers. Can today's children still relate? Maybe, but not very easily. It's a shame too. Most of them are well written, have wonderful characters</span>
  <span id="freeText11226148834945151260" style="display:none">1946 Newbery Medal winner.<br /><br />These older Newbery Medal books, these children's classics, are struggling to stand the test of time. Why? Well, take this one for example. It's about a time gone by, very different from today, a much harder time. It's characters, it's language, it's life situations are so stark, they must seem almost foreign to today's young readers. Can today's children still relate? Maybe, but not very easily. It's a shame too. Most of them are well written, have wonderful characters, and most share positive examples, themes and ideas that were important then and are still important today. About this book; I liked it. It's story line and themes are much more serious than you might guess from the title. Lenski was a good writer. She died in 1974 at age 80, and she published 98 books during that span.</span>

<div id="review_742718946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/742718946" />
    <a title="Craig Laurance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/136220-craig-laurance"><img alt="Craig Laurance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575599348p2/136220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/742718946?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Craig Laurance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Craig Laurance" href="/user/show/136220-craig-laurance">Craig Laurance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/136220-craig-laurance?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer742718946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12297276534904483734">Strawberry Girl was the first novel I read by children’s book author and illustrator Lois Lenski (October 14, 1893 – September 11, 1974). I read the book in the fifth grade in secret, because with its pink cover, not to mention title, was girly. At the time, I was in the process of reading books that had the Newbery Award, regardless of content. There were some duds in that bunch. For instance, I could not get into Dr. Doolittle by Hugh Lofting, due to the archaic language and the fact that ther</span>
  <span id="freeText12297276534904483734" style="display:none">Strawberry Girl was the first novel I read by children’s book author and illustrator Lois Lenski (October 14, 1893 – September 11, 1974). I read the book in the fifth grade in secret, because with its pink cover, not to mention title, was girly. At the time, I was in the process of reading books that had the Newbery Award, regardless of content. There were some duds in that bunch. For instance, I could not get into Dr. Doolittle by Hugh Lofting, due to the archaic language and the fact that there was a stereotypical black character.<br /><br />Strawberry Girl’s synopsis sounded girly, too. According to the back cover blurb, Birdie Boyer is a plucky ten-year old heroine in turn of the century Florida who oversees a crop of strawberries in the hopes of winning some Four H-styled prize. The actual story is somewhat darker. It’s about a Hatfield vs McCoyesque feud between the Boyer’s neighbors, who are in reality, squatters. The father, in particular, is a drunken lout with rage issues. The mother is not much better. The Boyers, by contrast, are one class above them, and while not educated, per se, have strong bourgeois values and a Puritan work ethic. The neighbors don’t resort to violence. Instead, they use criminal mischief, such as ignoring property boundaries and destroying crops. The neighbor’s son is the lone good egg in the family, and with the help of Birdie, tames his wild streak. The families enter into an uneasy truce, thanks to the friendship between the two kids. The story is accompanied by the author’s stark, black-and-white illustrations that have the austere quality of folk art.<br /><br />I ended up reading other Lenski books that year. Her regional series followed the lives of children in various US locales. Most of the scenarios dealt with poverty in some form or another. Appalachia is explored in Blue Ridge Billy. Judy’s Journey is about migrant workers. She even dealt with racism in a book that I only heard about, entitled Mama Hattie’s Girl, which features an all-African American (or in the parlance of the time, Negro) cast. Yet another novel is set in San Francisco’s Chinatown. Lenski was prolific, writing and illustrating many picture books, historical novels and even songbooks. Her focus on poverty and effects on children make her a kind of children’s lit version of John Steinbeck.<br /><br />Much of her work is out of print. This past summer, I volunteered for my local library (MLK Public Library here in DC), and I had the pleasure of working with the Rare Children’s Book Collection. Many Lenski works are housed in there.<br /><br />It’s a shame that more of her stuff isn’t in print. Her focus on the vulnerable left an impresseion my young mind, and made me empathetic and curious about the lives of others.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12297276534904483734" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review742718946">

  <span id="freeText6306075183755963404" style="display:none">I should have been more securely fastened in my chair when I finished this book - what a catapulting shock of an ending!! Christians, you'll LOVE IT!!<br /><br />I'm not sure how this book got missed in my childhood, but it's a sad occurrence for sure. The ending entirely made the book, and it's one that every Christian will applaud and cheer! So you're probably scratching your head like me, wondering just how this book won a Newbery Medal? I don't know. But here's what the story is about...<br /><br />A farming family moves to Florida in the hopes of doing better for themselves with a new plot of land and more opportunity. But will their neighbors allow it? Full of oneriness and spite, and a drunken father that eggs his children on, the neighbors are not the nice, friendly sort by any means. The family experiences one set back after another from the very people that live next to them. Will they be able to endure? <br /><br />You'll just have to read the book to see how it could possibly end with a shock!<br /><br />Ages: 6 - 12<br /><br />Cleanliness: "Law me" "shucks" and "Lawzy" are said. There is a scene with various people dancing. There is a drunk in the story who is changed. Two boys beat up the school teacher - he was so badly beaten that school is closed indefinitely. A girl gets so bad at a boy (that threw a snake at her) that she hates everything about him - she forgives him later. <br /><br />**Like my reviews? Then you should follow me! Because I have hundreds more just like this one. With each review, I provide a Cleanliness Report, mentioning any objectionable content I come across so that parents and/or conscientious readers (like me) can determine beforehand whether they want to read a book or not. Content surprises are super annoying, especially when you’re 100+ pages in, so here’s my attempt to help you avoid that! <br /><br />So Follow or Friend me here on GoodReads! You’ll see my updates as I’m reading and know which books I’m liking and what I’m not finishing and why. You’ll also be able to utilize my library for looking up titles to see whether the book you’re thinking about reading next has any objectionable content or not. From swear words, to romance, to bad attitudes (in children’s books), I cover it all!<br /></span>

<div id="review_2475110871" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2475110871" />
    <a title="ALLEN" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58158333-allen"><img alt="ALLEN" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578421145p2/58158333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2475110871?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ALLEN" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ALLEN" href="/user/show/58158333-allen">ALLEN</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2475110871" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8555473151868615217">Here's a great way to keep history alive for middle-schoolers. Lois Lenski wrote about ordinary country children, usually in agricultural occupations. Her STRAWBERRY GIRL lives in Florida and has to contend with rival families struggling to bring in the seasonal strawberry crop. While the time (ca. 1940) has now gone by, this is such a worthwhile document of Florida history that it is still in print and widely read in the Sunshine State. Perhaps your kids will enjoy it too! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3492651791" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3492651791" />
    <a title="Anna Mussmann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17812040-anna-mussmann"><img alt="Anna Mussmann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585698541p2/17812040.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3492651791?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Mussmann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Mussmann" href="/user/show/17812040-anna-mussmann">Anna Mussmann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3492651791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14147054361472130483">In her forward, Lenski explains that she writes novels about American children from different regions of our country so that young readers will know their land better. In particular, she wants to help American children to love those who are different from themselves by helping her readers understand each other better. <br/><br/>Even though she occasionally describes people with words or generalizations we wouldn’t find in a modern story, Lenski’s vintage books are a lovely example of a kind of “multicultu</span>
  <span id="freeText14147054361472130483" style="display:none">In her forward, Lenski explains that she writes novels about American children from different regions of our country so that young readers will know their land better. In particular, she wants to help American children to love those who are different from themselves by helping her readers understand each other better. <br /><br />Even though she occasionally describes people with words or generalizations we wouldn’t find in a modern story, Lenski’s vintage books are a lovely example of a kind of “multiculturalism” based on love and respect. <br /><br />In this novel, we witness the conflict between two contrasting households of Florida “crackers.” One family wants to fence their land and improve their lives through hard work and ingenuity. The other family violently resents anyone who restricts the free range of their cattle or who acts “uppity” by pursuing comfort or refinement of any kind. Nowadays we would say that the behavior and dynamics of the second family are definitely dysfunctional.<br /><br />In a modern story, I’m pretty sure that the father of the second family would be an irredeemable bad guy who needs to be kicked out by his wife. Yet that’s not Lenski’s approach at all. She is more interested in showing us these people in all their humanity than in judging them. In addition, the final solution is one that I cannot imagine appearing in a modern tale for children <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(this father is finally transformed by “getting saved” at a revival meeting after the preacher prays at him for a good long while! It's definitely a bit abrupt--definitely off-stage and a deus-ex-machina--but it fits the setting) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />I enjoyed this story and will be happy to share it with my children.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14147054361472130483" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2165136199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2165136199" />
    <a title="LaRae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6094388-larae"><img alt="LaRae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421290411p2/6094388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2165136199?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LaRae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LaRae" href="/user/show/6094388-larae">LaRae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6094388-larae?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6094388-larae?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2165136199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2708822423442601254">I really enjoyed this book. Not only are the characters well-drawn, and the illustrations quaint, but I learned a piece of Florida's history - something I knew nothing about prior to reading Strawberry Girl.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1711027458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1711027458" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1711027458?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1711027458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6823782783263633370"><br/>Ok, yes, I see that the other Slaters were ready to become 'civilized.' But their Pa's conversion, apparently by that hungry traveling preacher, as totally out-of-the-blue. This book is very much an earnest exhortation to hard work, clean living, and kindliness. Upon this reread, at this time of my life, it was almost nauseating.<br/><br/>I kept thinking, too, of the anthropological fallacy that Lenski succumbed to. It's clear that she can't but help think of herself as someone studying the natives, tryin</span>
  <span id="freeText6823782783263633370" style="display:none"><br />Ok, yes, I see that the other Slaters were ready to become 'civilized.' But their Pa's conversion, apparently by that hungry traveling preacher, as totally out-of-the-blue. This book is very much an earnest exhortation to hard work, clean living, and kindliness. Upon this reread, at this time of my life, it was almost nauseating.<br /><br />I kept thinking, too, of the anthropological fallacy that Lenski succumbed to. It's clear that she can't but help think of herself as someone studying the natives, trying to understand them well enough to improve them. Kindly meant, but unwelcome and foolish. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6729028.Vine_Deloria_Jr_" title="Vine Deloria Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Vine Deloria Jr.</a>, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/197753.Custer_Died_for_Your_Sins_An_Indian_Manifesto" title="Custer Died for Your Sins An Indian Manifesto by Vine Deloria Jr." rel="nofollow noopener">Custer Died for Your Sins: An Indian Manifesto</a> (and others) points out that people are very likely to lie to, and play tricks on, and keep secrets from, outsiders, especially the tactless and disrespectful. I just don't know how much of Lenski's portrait of 'Crackers' is authentic. Consider: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mediaite.com/online/cracker-means-something-entirely-different-in-florida-a-source-of-pride/">http://www.mediaite.com/online/cracke...</a><br /><br />The map is kinda-sorta funny, too. So much wilderness has been lost in Florida in such a short time.<br /><br />The time of this is still unclear, too. Here's a bit about the history of planting strawberries in Galloway: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://news.google.com/newspapers?nid=1346&amp;dat=19840314&amp;id=7dsvAAAAIBAJ&amp;sjid=mPsDAAAAIBAJ&amp;pg=6527,4792172&amp;hl=en">https://news.google.com/newspapers?ni...</a>. So, that supports the author's claim of sometime in the early 20th century. Perhaps studying the history of cattle ranching would give more precision - when did the open range give way to the fences? There's this: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.floridamemory.com/photographiccollection/photo_exhibits/ranching/ranching2.php">https://www.floridamemory.com/photogr...</a> which includes a photo of "First barbed wire fencing in Osceola County : Kissimmee, Florida (c. 1910)."</span>
  <a data-text-id="6823782783263633370" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_254006698" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/254006698" />
    <a title="Ruth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1436259-ruth"><img alt="Ruth" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/254006698?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ruth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ruth" href="/user/show/1436259-ruth">Ruth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer254006698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9474828821656435310">I like to think I've been reasonably successful in making readers out of my kids, though none of them loves it as much as I do. However, I haven't been terribly successful in passing on love of particular books. Strawberry Girl, along with Lois Lenski's other books about girls from various parts of the US, is one of those I loved but could never convince my older daughter to read. When NetGalley offered this one, I jumped at the chance to re-live part of my childhood (though I must admit that my</span>
  <span id="freeText9474828821656435310" style="display:none">I like to think I've been reasonably successful in making readers out of my kids, though none of them loves it as much as I do. However, I haven't been terribly successful in passing on love of particular books. Strawberry Girl, along with Lois Lenski's other books about girls from various parts of the US, is one of those I loved but could never convince my older daughter to read. When NetGalley offered this one, I jumped at the chance to re-live part of my childhood (though I must admit that my library has a large, though old set of Lenski's books). <br /><br />Strawberry Girl is set in the early 1900's in Florida when it was still a rural swamp. The main conflict is between a new family in town, a family that puts up fences and gardens and engages in agriculture as business, and a family that has been in town for a long time, or more precisely, the alcoholic father of that family, who is used to allowing his cattle and pigs to graze free and resents the fences the new people erect. This book, along with the others in the series, spotlights the differences in people's lives in various parts of the country prior to the homogenization wrought by television and big box retailers. Birdie and her family are "Crackers" and we learn the origin of the term. She attends a one-room school and goes barefoot most of the time. The dialogue in the book shows her dialect. They farm strawberries and oranges and drink milk from their own cow. Girls wear dresses made from flour sacks and get hats at the milliner. <br /><br />Any book that can still be found in libraries this many years after it was published has to appeal to someone besides just me, and it certainly appeals to me. It is a children's book--a quick Google search shows grade levels between 3 and 6. I give it an A.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9474828821656435310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_441262038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441262038" />
    <a title="Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4877911-ann"><img alt="Ann" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/441262038?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann" href="/user/show/4877911-ann">Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877911-ann?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877911-ann?shelf=newbery">newbery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4877911-ann?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441262038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer54244084945146352">This book almost rated four stars, but the highly improbably ending left a sour note in my mouth. I did not believe for a moment that a single kindness (even a long and sustained kindness) could so totally change the character of Mr. Slater. I could sort of see him being nice to the Boyers from now on, but his entire personality has changed. When he's talking about the death of his livlihood and entire way of life, it says that previously he'd have been in a rage, but now he was gentle as milk. </span>
  <span id="freeText54244084945146352" style="display:none">This book almost rated four stars, but the highly improbably ending left a sour note in my mouth. I did not believe for a moment that a single kindness (even a long and sustained kindness) could so totally change the character of Mr. Slater. I could sort of see him being nice to the Boyers from now on, but his entire personality has changed. When he's talking about the death of his livlihood and entire way of life, it says that previously he'd have been in a rage, but now he was gentle as milk. What? No. Having a change of heart, even a sincere one, does not change you completely overnight. He also seems to have kicked the alcoholism without any troubles whatsoever.<br /><br />I thought I was going to hate the dialect - I usually do - but I ended up really liking it. I think that was because it was largely a vocabulary difference rather than a pronunciation difference. I wasn't having to squint and think to figure out what a particular phonetic pile was meant to represent. A fair amount of the phrases, such as "might could" I have heard actual people use, so they were familiar to me already. <br /><br />The setting was one of the most distinguished characteristics of the book. The time period was one that I was not familiar with, particularly in a rural Florida context, and there were lots of details and atmosphere to make it come alive.<br /><br />Some of the pacing seemed almost episodic, a chapter would end with violence and the next one would open with something mundane. The little Slater girls were angry, then they weren't, then they were. But there are many other books set up like that, and I think it was purposeful. </span>
  <a data-text-id="54244084945146352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1288377745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1288377745" />
    <a title="Kathi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15239031-kathi"><img alt="Kathi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359513132p2/15239031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1288377745?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathi" href="/user/show/15239031-kathi">Kathi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15239031-kathi?shelf=newbery">newbery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288377745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1470602583161912653">This book is an example of an older Newbery that has not aged particularly well, but still offers very interesting glimpses of our American past.<br/><br/>Lois Lenski, prolific author of children’s books, wrote one large group of books about how children typically lived in different regions in the United States in the 1930s and 1940’s.<br/><br/>Strawberry Girl’s setting is Florida. It’s hard to believe that the rural dramas and the hard, hard lives depicted might have occurred where Disney World exists now! That fa</span>
  <span id="freeText1470602583161912653" style="display:none">This book is an example of an older Newbery that has not aged particularly well, but still offers very interesting glimpses of our American past.<br /><br />Lois Lenski, prolific author of children’s books, wrote one large group of books about how children typically lived in different regions in the United States in the 1930s and 1940’s.<br /><br />Strawberry Girl’s setting is Florida. It’s hard to believe that the rural dramas and the hard, hard lives depicted might have occurred where Disney World exists now! That fact alone adds interest to this 1946 Newbery winner.<br /><br />Other positives include the spunky central character of 10-year-old Birdie, strong and happy family values, and the persistency of her family to succeed in Florida. <br /><br />Negatives include jealous, nasty neighbors who not only mock the efforts of the Boyers, but actually commit dangerous criminal deeds to thwart their success. The scene that stays in my mind is one in which Birdie rides frantically to the Slaters’ house to beg them to help put out the brush fire that is creeping closer to their home. Mr. Slater and his sons just keep on rocking infuriatingly on their porch as Birdie realizes they purposefully set the fire. The misdeeds of these neighbors are treated rather nonchalantly, not with the condemnation they deserve.<br /><br />An equally big negative is the happy ending of the book. Although I generally love these, this ending is so unrealistic that I actually rolled my eyes many times during these pages. I am all for kindness and conversions, but the changes in the Slaters would have taken many miracles and months to convincingly occur.<br /><br />After reading Lois Lenski’s rich and impressive biographical sketch, I am certain that she deserves reading. I’m pretty sure, however, that she has better examples than Strawberry Girl. I also agree with Caitlin, my fellow Goodreader, that I wouldn't read this Lenski book to my (grand)children.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1470602583161912653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2250696293" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2250696293" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2250696293?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kailey (BooksforMKs)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kailey (BooksforMKs)" href="/user/show/5836046-kailey-booksformks">Kailey (BooksforMKs)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/12042165-strawberry-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5836046-kailey-booksformks?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2250696293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10179487944242605301">I liked this book about a family who moves to a new farm in Florida, during the pioneer days, determined to make the farm a success with a beautiful orchard and strawberry grove. <br/>Birdie is excited to become a Strawberry Girl, but is worried that the disgruntled neighbors will make trouble for her family. When the neighbor's pigs and cows trample over the new strawberry plants, Birdie's father is outraged and vows to fence in his property to keep them out. This begins a feud between the two farme</span>
  <span id="freeText10179487944242605301" style="display:none">I liked this book about a family who moves to a new farm in Florida, during the pioneer days, determined to make the farm a success with a beautiful orchard and strawberry grove. <br />Birdie is excited to become a Strawberry Girl, but is worried that the disgruntled neighbors will make trouble for her family. When the neighbor's pigs and cows trample over the new strawberry plants, Birdie's father is outraged and vows to fence in his property to keep them out. This begins a feud between the two farmers, but the farmer's children are eager to make friends. Only Birdie and her forgiving mother can make peace between the warring neighbors, and make both farms a success!<br /><br />I loved the authentic accents and idiomatic dialogue of the characters, and the rich history presented in this story! It's also special to know that most of the stories here are true, and really happened to various pioneers, cattlemen, and farmers in those days.<br /><br />This book reminds me strongly on the Little House on the Prairie series, but it's missing the enchanting writing and I didn't really identify or connect with the characters in this book as much as with Little House. The characters in this story are too ornery! I enjoyed reading this story, but it just can't compare to Little House. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10179487944242605301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria" href="/user/show/3412574-victoria">Victoria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3412574-victoria?shelf=books-i-ve-read">books-i-ve-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2170540278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15491361678481574799">This book started out okay, and I like the fact that the author did research on a group of people that were little known about, but I feel the stories didn't really captivate me. Perhaps it is because I am older now in reading a children's story, but I just feel like I was not charmed or able to gain an attachment for the main characters. <br/><br/>This is about people who lived in a remote area of Florida during the 1940s, but who still were living in a more colonial way. The whole story is about the Boy</span>
  <span id="freeText15491361678481574799" style="display:none">This book started out okay, and I like the fact that the author did research on a group of people that were little known about, but I feel the stories didn't really captivate me. Perhaps it is because I am older now in reading a children's story, but I just feel like I was not charmed or able to gain an attachment for the main characters. <br /><br />This is about people who lived in a remote area of Florida during the 1940s, but who still were living in a more colonial way. The whole story is about the Boyer family and their mean neighbors the Slater family, though really it is just that the Slater father is a drunk who takes it out on his family and neighbors a lot. We have such a strange feud to read about in this book that these neighbors are shooting one another's animals, burning their land, spanking their children, and more. I feel this book was really just a depressing story. The end has a happier note, but it doesn't make up for the fact that this is just too sad for a children's story. . . .I mean two of the Slater sons even beat up their own teacher nearly to death. It is really crazy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15491361678481574799" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1055007948876642047">Backwoods Florida sounds to be as rough and tumble as the wild west. They had the same problems with ranging cattle ... and what about those "biggety" folk who come from the North (that is, "Caroliny") with their annoying habits, such as attending school, actually feeding their livestock, planting crops, painting their houses, putting up fences to keep the friendly neighborhood livestock from destroying their crops, and going to church. <br/>I don't want to give anything away, but I would have prefer</span>
  <span id="freeText1055007948876642047" style="display:none">Backwoods Florida sounds to be as rough and tumble as the wild west. They had the same problems with ranging cattle ... and what about those "biggety" folk who come from the North (that is, "Caroliny") with their annoying habits, such as attending school, actually feeding their livestock, planting crops, painting their houses, putting up fences to keep the friendly neighborhood livestock from destroying their crops, and going to church. <br />I don't want to give anything away, but I would have preferred for Pa Slater to have been eaten by a 'gator. First of all, it has a nice rhyme to it. Secondly, he's a right bastard and deserves it.<br />The pictures are charming, and the big strawberry tray on the cover reminds me of my dad's homemade toolbox. Now I wonder if that has anything to do with his family having raised strawberries. Boy, those bonnets sure were big!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64816879?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deb (Readerbuzz) Nance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deb (Readerbuzz) Nance" href="/user/show/1654645-deb-readerbuzz-nance">Deb (Readerbuzz) Nance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1654645-deb-readerbuzz-nance?shelf=newbery">newbery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1654645-deb-readerbuzz-nance?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64816879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8671189582792947990">How could a child read this book and complain about her life in 21st century America? The two families in this book suffer from the ravages of grasshoppers, illness, hunger, and jealousy. They argue and fight with each other, eventually going so far as to kill each other’s animals and set fire to the other’s farmhouse. A hardscrabble life complete with rattlesnakes and alligators and swamps. Yet there was also a beauty to this life, of neighbors helping each other, even when they have little for</span>
  <span id="freeText8671189582792947990" style="display:none">How could a child read this book and complain about her life in 21st century America? The two families in this book suffer from the ravages of grasshoppers, illness, hunger, and jealousy. They argue and fight with each other, eventually going so far as to kill each other’s animals and set fire to the other’s farmhouse. A hardscrabble life complete with rattlesnakes and alligators and swamps. Yet there was also a beauty to this life, of neighbors helping each other, even when they have little for themselves. Some unbelievable elements---an alcoholic dad suddenly stops drinking and a child who never seems to do anything worse than get a little mad now and then---but all in all a worthwhile read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8671189582792947990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1148152466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1148152466" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1531905-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227028718p2/1531905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1148152466?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/1531905-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1531905-lisa?shelf=children-s-fiction">children-s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1531905-lisa?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1531905-lisa?shelf=newbery-winner">newbery-winner</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1148152466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9977026697703502776">This was a surprising read for me. I didn't know that Lois Lenski has an "American Regional Series" set in various parts of the US, highlighting childhood in such parts. Strawberry Girl is set in the pioneer days of Florida and seen through the eyes of young Birdie Boyer whose family settles in the backwoods. In a way, this book shows signs of age but it is so well told that I believe it would make a great read-aloud as long as the reader is committed to reading the dialogue in the backwoods dia</span>
  <span id="freeText9977026697703502776" style="display:none">This was a surprising read for me. I didn't know that Lois Lenski has an "American Regional Series" set in various parts of the US, highlighting childhood in such parts. Strawberry Girl is set in the pioneer days of Florida and seen through the eyes of young Birdie Boyer whose family settles in the backwoods. In a way, this book shows signs of age but it is so well told that I believe it would make a great read-aloud as long as the reader is committed to reading the dialogue in the backwoods dialect. I learned a lot about Florida that I didn't know and the fencing (or non-fencing) of cattle, too;) I think it's notable that Lenski took the time to consider the makings of childhood in more than one location.<br /><br />I'm going to read the Appalachian, Blue Ridge Billy next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9977026697703502776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2365367302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365367302" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50448-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1175789489p2/50448.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365367302?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/50448-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=operationactuallybooks">operationactuallybooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2018goodrule-old">2018goodrule-old</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50448-becky?shelf=2018reviews">2018reviews</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365367302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer746651710760367961">First sentence: 'That goes our cow, Pa!' said the little girl.<br/><br/>Premise/plot: The Boyer family has newly moved into the community. Most make the family feel welcome. Not so their nearest neighbors the Slaters. From the start these two families clash. Birdie Boyer, for example, clashes with Shoestring. The Slater mother has a love-to-hate, hate-to-love relationship with the Boyer mother. She tends to think that the Boyers are uppity SNOBS because they have (relatively) nice things. The two fathers,</span>
  <span id="freeText746651710760367961" style="display:none">First sentence: 'That goes our cow, Pa!' said the little girl.<br /><br />Premise/plot: The Boyer family has newly moved into the community. Most make the family feel welcome. Not so their nearest neighbors the Slaters. From the start these two families clash. Birdie Boyer, for example, clashes with Shoestring. The Slater mother has a love-to-hate, hate-to-love relationship with the Boyer mother. She tends to think that the Boyers are uppity SNOBS because they have (relatively) nice things. The two fathers, well, that's simpler. They can't stand each other--at all.<br /><br />Can the Boyer family live out the teaching LOVE YOUR NEIGHBOR AS YOURSELF? Or will the Slaters' hateful actions prove too much to bear?<br /><br />This pioneer novel is set in the early twentieth century in Florida. Irritable neighbors aren't the only difficulty they face on the farm.<br /><br />It was written and illustrated by Lois Lenski. It won the Newbery in 1946.<br /><br />My thoughts: I really ended up loving Strawberry Girl. I wish I'd listened to my mother decades ago when she tried to encourage me to read it.<br /><br />I wasn't expecting such a spiritual message in Strawberry Girl. I was pleasantly surprised by the themes of redemption and grace. The last chapter was giddy making.<br /><blockquote><br />“You have heard that it was said, ‘You shall love your neighbor and hate your enemy.’ But I say to you, love your enemies and pray for those who persecute you, so that you may be sons of your Father who is in heaven; for He causes His sun to rise on the evil and the good, and sends rain on the righteous and the unrighteous. For if you love those who love you, what reward do you have? Do not even the tax collectors do the same? If you greet only your brothers, what more are you doing than others? Do not even the Gentiles do the same? Therefore you are to be perfect, as your heavenly Father is perfect. Matthew 5:43-48<br />For the whole Law is fulfilled in one word, in the statement, “You shall love your neighbor as yourself.” But if you bite and devour one another, take care that you are not consumed by one another. Galatians 5:14-15<br />A new commandment I give to you, that you love one another, even as I have loved you, that you also love one another. By this all men will know that you are My disciples, if you have love for one another. John 13:34-35</blockquote><br /><blockquote><br />"Glory hallelujah!" cried Sam Slater, throwing his hat in the air. "I'm a changed man! A happy man for the first time in my life!" "Brother Jackson shore is a powerful preacher," said Mrs. Boyer."To touch the heart of a hardened sinner like me," added Slater.<br />"I mean no offense..." began Mrs. Boyer.<br />"But hit's true ain't it?" said Slater gently. "My heart was hard as a rock. Now 'tis soft as mud. I'll never the same again, thank God."<br />"How did it happen, Sam?" asked Boyer. "Tell us about it." Sam Slater grew thoughtful, then he spoke: "When I come home and found my wife and young guns had been lying' at death's door, I begun to think. Did I not have kind, forgivin' neighbors, they'd a been dead. Then the very next night I got sick myself, and thought I was fixin' to die. So I decided I'd better start livin' different. But it was Brother Jackson who pointed out the error of my ways. He told me the harm of drinkin' liquor, and of swearin' and backbitin', gossip and anger. So when the spirit come upon me, I was ready. My heart was changed. I'm fixin' to lead the good life right on."<br />"Praise God!" cried the women.<br />"Glory be to God!" added the men.<br />"You won't never get drunk no more, Pa?" asked Essie.<br />"And shoot the chickens' heads off, Pa?" asked Zephy.<br />"No young guns, I won't!" said Sam Slater. He took the two little girls in his arms and held them close. "And I hope to be a good neighbor right on, too. A good father and a good neighbor." (185-86) </blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="746651710760367961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_158194395" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/158194395" />
    <a title="Jen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/588645-jen"><img alt="Jen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419900874p2/588645.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/158194395?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen" href="/user/show/588645-jen">Jen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780397301096" href="/book/show/2860940-strawberry-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/588645-jen?shelf=newbery">newbery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/588645-jen?shelf=kids">kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer158194395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2331019362608646850">Charming in the order of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/205821.Caddie_Woodlawn' title='Caddie Woodlawn by Carol Ryrie Brink' rel='nofollow noopener'>Caddie Woodlawn</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/854764.Thimble_Summer' title='Thimble Summer by Elizabeth Enright' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thimble Summer</a>. Birdie and the other characters are as complex as can be expected. I enjoyed Lenski's description of the setting. As I've never been to that part of Florida, I appreciated "hearing" their speech and "seeing" their homes. In the foreward, Lenski mentions having visited Florida and spending time with the people she would write about. It seems she wanted to write stories set in a variety of communities in the States, so that Americans coul</span>
  <span id="freeText2331019362608646850" style="display:none">Charming in the order of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/205821.Caddie_Woodlawn" title="Caddie Woodlawn by Carol Ryrie Brink" rel="nofollow noopener">Caddie Woodlawn</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/854764.Thimble_Summer" title="Thimble Summer by Elizabeth Enright" rel="nofollow noopener">Thimble Summer</a>. Birdie and the other characters are as complex as can be expected. I enjoyed Lenski's description of the setting. As I've never been to that part of Florida, I appreciated "hearing" their speech and "seeing" their homes. In the foreward, Lenski mentions having visited Florida and spending time with the people she would write about. It seems she wanted to write stories set in a variety of communities in the States, so that Americans could get to know one another in a way. I kinda like that.<br /><br />The last couple chapters were a bit awkward and rushed as she tied up some loose ends and "redeemed" some of the characters in a way that felt contrived and clumsy, whereas the majority of the story followed as least some sort of an arc. <br /><br />It'd be fun to read with young kids and is probably one of the better Newbery winners of its time, but there's not much else to say about it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2331019362608646850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498456279?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juli Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juli Anna" href="/user/show/18571740-juli-anna">Juli Anna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18571740-juli-anna?shelf=kidlit">kidlit</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498456279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13679573838084401864">This one actually grew on me as I was reading--it gets 2 1/2 stars. Heavy dialect is always difficult for me to get through without rolling my eyes (it usually just feels so contrived and culturally insensitive), and this was no exception. It's also very strange subject matter for a children's book; it's the story of an escalating feud between two families in rural Florida. As the book got weirder ("Pa done got drunk and shot all the heads off Ma's chickens jest to see iffen he could hit um") I </span>
  <span id="freeText13679573838084401864" style="display:none">This one actually grew on me as I was reading--it gets 2 1/2 stars. Heavy dialect is always difficult for me to get through without rolling my eyes (it usually just feels so contrived and culturally insensitive), and this was no exception. It's also very strange subject matter for a children's book; it's the story of an escalating feud between two families in rural Florida. As the book got weirder ("Pa done got drunk and shot all the heads off Ma's chickens jest to see iffen he could hit um") I liked it more and by the end, I could appreciate it as a work of Realism, though the surprise ending about knocked my socks off. Overall, strange and dated, but not a poor addition to the Newbery canon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13679573838084401864" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2736057082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2736057082" />
    <a title="jiji" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2605280-jiji"><img alt="jiji" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530894431p2/2605280.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2736057082?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jiji" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jiji" href="/user/show/2605280-jiji">jiji</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13339577-strawberry-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2605280-jiji?shelf=children-s-books">children-s-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2605280-jiji?shelf=women-writers">women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2605280-jiji?shelf=ya-historical-fiction">ya-historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2605280-jiji?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2736057082&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2736057082" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10733074403129625024">I've been a little (a lot) obsessed with Florida for the last few months, ever since I found out that Lauren Groff lives in Gainesville, Florida. For months, I've been pondering the following question: What would lead a writer to choose Florida as their home? Especially Gainesville, which appears to be a small city somewhere in the middle of Florida and not particularly close to any beach? Don’t writers need mountains or shimmering cities for inspiration? This curiosity lead to my read lots of b</span>
  <span id="freeText10733074403129625024" style="display:none">I've been a little (a lot) obsessed with Florida for the last few months, ever since I found out that Lauren Groff lives in Gainesville, Florida. For months, I've been pondering the following question: What would lead a writer to choose Florida as their home? Especially Gainesville, which appears to be a small city somewhere in the middle of Florida and not particularly close to any beach? Don’t writers need mountains or shimmering cities for inspiration? This curiosity lead to my read lots of books either by Florida authors (Vampires in the Lemon Grove, Delicate Edible Birds) or set in Florida (Turtle in Paradise, Raymie Nightingale, Because of Winn-Dixie). In the last few days, my obsession has become so acute that I actually ended up buying tickets to Florida, and now I’m going to St. Petersburg for a week in April. I want to experience Florida for myself. I want mangroves, swamps, boardwalks, humidity, palm trees, kitsch (lots and lots of kitsch), roadside attractions, tiki bars, Margaritas, fanny packs, beach umbrellas, strip mall cities…I want it all. Anyway, all this to say that I stumbled on this book in the midst of my obsession and that's how I ended up reading a children’s novel I'd never heard of by an author I’d never heard of. Set in the backwoods of Central Florida? I was sold. <br /><br />It appears that children's books, like Disney movies, have changed significantly. I can't imagine any author being able to publish a book like this nowadays. This was a Newbury winner, but it hasn’t aged all that well. It’s raucous. Its characters are mean-spirited. It’s dark in a folksy way. The dialect is a little too rich sometimes. The level of animal cruelty is cringe-worthy. It’s barely redemptive. We don’t expose our children to these kinds of stories anymore, at least not on purpose. This book is not enlightened. But I still liked it. The wild west has nothing on the swampy hinterlands of early 20th century Florida. <br /><br />The Boyers and Slaters are neighbors. The Slaters are Florida "crackers" (Lenski’s words, not mine) illegally squatting on their land and running their cattle anywhere they please. They are crass, entitled and not particularly reflective. As a mental health professional, I would say the family dynamic is likely the result of generational trauma, addiction and dysfunction. Pa Slater is a mean drunk. He’s abusive. He lets his family go hungry while he goes on drinking and gambling binges. Oh...Pa Slater also tries to burn his neighbor's house down and poisons the Boyers' family mule. Why, you ask, does he hate his neighbors so much? Because they are uppity northerners from “Caroliny” who fence in their land, thus inhibiting his cattle’s free range foraging. <br />But before you start feeling too sorry for the Boyer family, you should keep in mind that Pa Boyer is no angel either. As Mrs. Boyer would say, he likes to cause a "ruckus," and both Pa Slater and Pa Boyer seem to fully embrace an eye-for-an-eye mentality. Mr. Boyer chops the ears off Pa Slater's hogs. After Pa Slater strikes back, Mr. Boyer retaliates by upping the ante and killing three of Pa Slater's hogs. This is the way the story goes for about 180 pages. This book might be called “Strawberry Girl,” but it really should be called “The Great Slater-Boyer War,” or something like that. Birdie, the so-called main character, as well as her strawberries, are really secondary to the epic battle between the Slater and Boyer patriarchs. <br /><br />In the last few pages, Pa Slater’s hardened stone of a heart is softened by the ministrations of a sketchy and ravenous traveling preacher man who introduces him to the healing powers of religion. Suddenly, Pa Slater turns into a soft-hearted, stand-up kind of guy. The neighbor wars are over. He sells his cattle. He stops drinking. He stops beating his wife and kids. The kids go to school to get an education. All is well. The unruly, wild, horrible Slaters have been tamed. <br />I would like to point out that when Pa Slater’s son, Shoestring Slater (who hasn’t eaten a meal in a week) complains after the visiting preacher eats two whole chickens leaving no meat for Shoestring or his starving siblings, the preacher says, and I quote: “Take that boy out and whop him!” That’ll learn him to be mannerly!” Ha!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10733074403129625024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2246900736" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2246900736" />
    <a title="Alexandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4538194-alexandra"><img alt="Alexandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599115695p2/4538194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2246900736?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexandra" href="/user/show/4538194-alexandra">Alexandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13339577-strawberry-girl">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2246900736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13352119097453196223">🍓🍓this popped up in my recommendations on amazon & i figured i would give it a try. the illustration on the cover reminded me a lot of my beloved betsy-tacy treasury that i read when i was a kid, and i was hoping strawberry girl would be something like that. quaint, sweet, feel-good. <br/><br/>what i wasn't expecting was how gritty it would be! sure, yes it was quaint. i mean, it takes place in the backwoods of florida in 1900. but it was...dark too. for example the main character birdie wasn't just a hap</span>
  <span id="freeText13352119097453196223" style="display:none">🍓🍓this popped up in my recommendations on amazon &amp; i figured i would give it a try. the illustration on the cover reminded me a lot of my beloved betsy-tacy treasury that i read when i was a kid, and i was hoping strawberry girl would be something like that. quaint, sweet, feel-good. <br /><br />what i wasn't expecting was how gritty it would be! sure, yes it was quaint. i mean, it takes place in the backwoods of florida in 1900. but it was...dark too. for example the main character birdie wasn't just a happy go lucky kid milking cows and picking strawberries. <br /><br />she was babysitting for all her younger siblings, working the fields, and having to contend with some pretty awful neighbors who would cut down her family's fences and let their cows trample the fields and crops; leave threatening notes; allows their hogs on her family's property who would eat everything up and make a mess of things. <br /><br />birdie was in the middle of what was basically a huge rivalry between her family and her neighbors. <br />i mean, there were pigs ears getting chopped off and verbal threats made. this is a kids book but it's not necessarily a fun one to get through:/<br /><br />the treatment of animals in this book really upset me. for example, the slaters don't feed their cows at all and leave them to forage. and shoestring slater catches all kinds of wild animals like raccoons and puts leashes on them and tries to make them his pet. he catches a wild rattlesnake and puts it in a cage with a live rabbit 😓 (i have rabbits so this one made me especially sad). and also, he catches tortoises and then stands on their back while "racing" them. it's cruel...<br />also when the fighting between the neighbors got bad, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[animals actually got killed. mr. boyer killed 3 of slater's hogs &amp; then to retaliate, slater killed their mule by poisoning it. just barbaric 😪 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />i mean i know the author was trying to portray what times were like back then, and maybe this is true to form, but it's still unfortunate and sad 😪<br /><br />i did really appreciate the locale and time period of this story (as well as the thoughtful foreword from the author in the beginning). i don't think i've ever read anything set in florida in the early 1900's and it was interesting to learn about the "Crackers" and read dialogue that was written colloquially in the way that they spoke. <br /><br />i can't see many youngsters today getting into a book like this willingly...unless they had a particular affinity for history. 🍓🍓<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13352119097453196223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+H7wG0r7ICtDyyzjRzVtfla0Djpz7ehYmGN8jtwHBl6pY1WD/lx1O3NbCTYeVA8IdOJL1oTBFGqRCCMlJI1chw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PLI9FBwj4UqZlQA+0hu9XIExrWz2emA+tiNsKPK5E4Btr5iMqIS0WqkFJeuLet8qo2fogAFWnAy/SDODCjNJWQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer13168022390556625704"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lois_Lenski'>http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lois_Lenski</a><br/><br/>Many of Lenski's books can be collated into 'series' - but since they don't have to be read in order, you may be better off just looking for more information here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://library.illinoisstate.edu/unique-collections/lois-lenski/work.php'>http://library.illinoisstate.edu/uniq...</a><br/><br/>Probably her most famous set is the following:<br/>American Regional Series<br/><br/>Beginning with Bayou Suzette in 1943, Lois Lenski began writing a series of books whic</span>
  <span id="freeText13168022390556625704" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lois_Lenski">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lois_Lenski</a><br /><br />Many of Lenski's books can be collated into 'series' - but since they don't have to be read in order, you may be better off just looking for more information here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://library.illinoisstate.edu/unique-collections/lois-lenski/work.php">http://library.illinoisstate.edu/uniq...</a><br /><br />Probably her most famous set is the following:<br />American Regional Series<br /><br />Beginning with Bayou Suzette in 1943, Lois Lenski began writing a series of books which would become known as her "regional series." In the early 1940s Lenski, who suffered from periodic bouts of ill-health, was told by her doctor that she needed to spend the winter months in a warmer climate than her Connecticut home. As a result, Lenski and her husband Arthur Covey traveled south each fall. Lenski wrote in her autobiography, "On my trips south I saw the real America for the first time. I saw and learned what the word region meant as I witnessed firsthand different ways of life unlike my own. What interested me most was the way children were living" (183).<br />In Journey Into Childhood, Lenski wrote that she was struck by the fact that there were "plenty of books that tell how children live in Alaska, Holland, China, and Mexico, but no books at all telling about the many ways children live here in the United States" <br /><br />Bayou Suzette. <br />Strawberry Girl.<br />Blue Ridge Billy.<br />Judy's Journey. <br />Boom Town Boy.<br />Cotton in My Sack. <br />Texas Tomboy.<br />Prairie School. <br />Corn-Farm Boy. <br />San Francisco Boy. <br />Flood Friday. <br />Houseboat Girl. <br />Coal Camp Girl. <br />Shoo-Fly Girl.<br />To Be a Logger. <br />Deer Valley Girl.<br /></span>

    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
